- [00:00] In the early 1800's, German physician, Franz Joseph Gall spent a lot of time running his
- [00:05] fingers over the scalps of strangers. He wasn't a hairdresser, he wasn't a masseuse, he wasn't
- [00:11] just like a big fan of heads. He was a phrenologist, he was the first phrenologist. Gall believed
- [00:16] that a persons personality was linked to their skull morphology, that its bumps and ridges
- [00:21] indicated aspects of their character. Amazingly this "science" actually caught on, was widely
- [00:26] practiced for decades, and Gall became something of a celebrity.
- [00:30] Well, with a head like his, one can see how he might have been a little bit fixated with
- [00:35] skull shape.

- [00:40] cranial contours tell us exactly nothing about what's happening inside the brain.

- [00:57] was that different parts of the brain control specific aspects of our behavior.
